He was skilled, humble, and compassionate cardiologist who was loved by the hospital staff, medical staff members and certainly his patients. He held numerous hospital leadership positions and committee appointments in the SouthEast Region. . Dr. Cayenne was a kind and compassionate father, son, brother, husband, and physician. Whether it is reflections from his friends, family or patients, he is remembered and revered for his humility, warmth, kindness, and patience. His dedication to people was reflected not only in his choice of profession but his relentless dedication to treating everyone with equality and acceptance. We are all fortunate to have known such an incredible human being. . Please keep his two sons Samir Cayenne and Sanal Cayenne as well as his wife Chandra Kaipa in your prayers. . Please join his Family in celebrating the life of Dr Satish Cayenne at the First Church of Pearland on Saturday, May 4. Navajo Code Talker Begaye is Tódích’íi’nii (Bitter Water Clan) and born for Kinłichii’nii (Red House People Clan). He was born on August 26, 1921 in the community of Red Valley, Arizona and resided in Chinle, Arizona at the time of his passing. He had three children with his late wife, Helen M. Begaye, who passed away in 2008.\nBegaye served as a Navajo Code Talker in the Marine Corps from 1943 to 1945, and fought in the Battle of Tarawa and the Batter of Tinian and later spent one year in a naval hospital as a result of injuries and wounds he received during his service.\n----------------------------------------------------------\nLess than 7 Navajo Code Talkers are left of the 400+ who served. We should give no quarter to the political elite who normalize and erase the violence extractive capitalism brings to our communities.
